Question: The first year Eleanor organized a fund-raising event, she invited 30 people. For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year. If $f(n)$ is the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event, which of the following statements best describes the function $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: The function $f$ is a decreasing linear function.
  B: The function $f$ is an increasing linear function.
  C: The function $f$ is a decreasing exponential function.
  D: The function $f$ is an increasing exponential function.
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  - For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year.
  - Let's call the number of people Eleanor invited in year $n$ as $x_n$. Then, we have:
    - $x_1 = 30$
    - $x_2 = 2x_1 = 60$
    - $x_3 = 2x_2 = 120$
    - $x_4 = 2x_3 = 240$
    - $x_5 = 2x_4 = 480$
    - $x_6 = 2x_5 = 960$
  - We can see that the function $f$ is not linear, because the rate of increase is not constant. Instead, it is increasing exponentially, because the number of people invited each year is being multiplied by a constant factor of 2.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  - In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people.
  - For each of the next 5 years, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year.
  - Let $f(n)$ be the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event.

    - $f(1) = 30$
    - $f(2) = 2f(1) = 60$
    - $f(3) = 2f(2) = 2(2f(1)) = 2^2f(1) = 120$
    - $f(4) = 2f(3) = 2(2^2f(1)) = 2^3f(1) = 240$
    - $f(5) = 2f(4) = 2(2^3f(1)) = 2^4f(1) = 480$
    - We can see that $f(n)$ is an increasing exponential function with a base of 2.

  - $f(n)$ is the number of people invited to the fund-raiser $n$ years after Eleanor began organizing the event.
  
Analysis:
  - In the first year, Eleanor invited 30 people, so $f(1) = 30$.
  - In the second year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, so $f(2) = 2 \cdot f(1)$.
  - In the third year, she invited double the number of people she had invited the previous year, so $f(3) = 2 \cdot f(2) = 2 \cdot 2 \cdot f(1) = 2^2 \cdot f(1)$.

  - Therefore, we can write $f(n) = 2^{n-1} \cdot f(1)$ for $n \geq 1$.
  - This is an increasing exponential function, since the base of the exponent (2) is greater than 1, and the coefficient ($f(1)$) is positive.

Question: Survey Results\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}\hlineAnswer & Percent \\\hlineNever & $31.3 \%$ \\\hlineRarely & $24.3 \%$ \\\hlineOften & $13.5 \%$ \\\hlineAlways & $30.9 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows the results of a survey in which tablet users were asked how often they would watch video advertisements in order to access streaming content for free. Based on the table, which of the following is closest to the probability that a tablet user answered "Always," given that the tablet user did not answer "Never"?
Choices:
  A: 0.31
  B: 0.38
  C: 0.45
  D: 0.69
Response 0:
Let's first calculate the probability of a tablet user not answering "Never". This is the sum of the percentages for "Rarely", "Often", and "Always": $24.3 \% + 13.5 \% + 30.9 \% = 68.7 \%$. 

Now, we want to find the probability that a tablet user answered "Always" given that they did not answer "Never". This is the percentage of tablet users who answered "Always" out of the percentage who did not answer "Never". 

The percentage of tablet users who answered "Always" is $30.9 \%$. The percentage of tablet users who did not answer "Never" is $68.7 \%$. So, the probability that a tablet user answered "Always" given that they did not answer "Never" is:

$$\frac{30.9 \%}{68.7 \%} \approx 0.45$$

Therefore, the closest answer is (C) 0.45. 

Action: Answer("C")

  The probability of a tablet user answering "Always" is $30.9 \%$.

Now, we want to find the probability that a tablet user answered "Always" given that they did not answer "Never". We can calculate this using conditional probability:

$$P(\text{Always}|\text{not Never}) = \frac{P(\text{Always and not Never})}{P(\text{not Never})}$$

We can find $P(\text{Always and not Never})$ by multiplying the percentage of users who answered "Always" by the percentage of users who did not answer "Never":

$$P(\text{Always and not Never}) = 30.9 \% \times 68.7 \% = 21.2 \%$$

We already calculated that $P(\text{not Never}) = 68.7 \%$. 

Now we can substitute these values into the conditional probability formula:

$$P(\text{Always}|\text{not Never}) = \frac{21.2 \%}{68.7 \%} \approx 0.3088 \approx 0.31$$

So the closest answer choice is (A) 0.31.

    1. Marisa needs to hire at least 10 staff members: $x + y \geq 10$
    2. She must hire at least 3 junior directors: $x \geq 3$
    3. She must hire at least 1 senior director: $y \geq 1$
    4. The budget for paying the staff members is no more than $\$ 9,700$ per week: $640x + 880y \leq 9700$
    
Solution:
  The correct system of inequalities is:
  $640x + 880y \leq 9700$
  $x + y \geq 10$
  $x \geq 3$
  $y \geq 1$

Question: A line in the $x y$-plane passes through the origin and has a slope of $\frac{1}{7}$. Which of the following points lies on the line?
Choices:
  A: $(0,7)$
  B: $(1,7)$
  C: $(7,7)$
  D: $(14,2)$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The equation of a line in slope-intercept form is $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the $y$-intercept.
  If the line passes through the origin, then the $y$-intercept is 0.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $y=\frac{1}{7}x$.
  A: If $x=0$, then $y=0$, so $(0,7)$ is not on the line.
  B: If $x=1$, then $y=\frac{1}{7}\cdot 1=\frac{1}{7}$, so $(1,7)$ is not on the line.
  C: If $x=7$, then $y=\frac{1}{7}\cdot 7=1$, so $(7,7)$ is not on the line.
  D: If $x=14$, then $y=\frac{1}{7}\cdot 14=2$, so $(14,2)$ is on the line.
Action: Answer("D")

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Jennifer bought a box of Crunchy Grain cereal. The nutrition facts on the box state that a serving size of the cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat. In addition, each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
Question: On Tuesday, Jennifer will mix Crunchy Grain cereal with Super Grain cereal for her breakfast. Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup. If the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, how much Super Grain cereal is in one cup of the mixture?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$
  C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$
  D: $\frac{1}{2} \operatorname{cup}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories.
  Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 50 calories from fat.
  Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
  One cup of Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories.
  The total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270.
Action: 
Let's assume that Jennifer mixes $x$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $y$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal. 
From the given information, we know that the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270. Therefore, we can write the following equation:
$240x + \frac{210}{\frac{3}{4}}y = 270$
Simplifying the above equation, we get:
$240x + 280y = 810$
We also know that a serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, which means that one cup of Crunchy Grain cereal provides:
$\frac{210}{\frac{3}{4}} = 280$ calories
Therefore, the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture that come from Crunchy Grain cereal is $280y$.
Since the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, we can write the following equation:
$240x + 280y = 270$
Solving for $x$, we get:
$x = \frac{27 - 7y}{24}$
We know that Jennifer mixes Crunchy Grain cereal and Super Grain cereal in the ratio of $\frac{y}{x}$ to $\frac{1}{1}$, which means that:
$\frac{y}{x+1} = \frac{y}{\frac{27-7y}{24}+1} = \frac{y}{\frac{51-7y}{24}}$
We are given that the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, which means that:
$240x + 280y = 270$
$240\left(\frac{27-7y}{24}\right) + 280y = 270$
Simplifying the above equation, we get:
$y = \frac{3}{2}$
Therefore, the amount of Super Grain cereal in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is:
$x = \frac{27 - 7y}{24} = \frac{27 - 7\left(\frac{3}{2}\right)}{24} = \frac{1}{4}$
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - A serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat.
  - Each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
  - Jennifer's mixture contains Crunchy Grain cereal and Super Grain cereal.
  - Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup.
  - The total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270.
  
Calculations:
  - Let's assume that Jennifer mixes $x$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $y$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal.
  - We know that the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270. Therefore, we can write the following equation:
    $$240x + \frac{210}{\frac{3}{4}}y = 270$$
  - Simplifying the equation, we get:
    $$240x + 280y = 810$$
  - We also know that a serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories. Therefore, we can write the following equation:
    $$\frac{210}{\frac{3}{4}}y = 280y = \text{total number of calories from Crunchy Grain cereal in one cup of Jennifer's mixture}$$
  - We can now write an equation for the total number of calories from Super Grain cereal in one cup of Jennifer's mixture:
    $$240x = \text{total number of calories from Super Grain cereal in one cup of Jennifer's mixture}$$
  - We want to find the amount of Super Grain cereal in one cup of the mixture, which is represented by $x$. We can solve for $x$ by using the equation $240x + 280y = 810$ and the fact that the total amount of cereal in one cup of the mixture is $x+y=1$. Solving for $x$, we get:
    $$x = \frac{810-280y}{240} = \frac{27}{8} - \frac{7}{6}y$$
  - We know that $x$ must be positive, so we can set the inequality $\frac{27}{8} - \frac{7}{6}y > 0$ and solve for $y$:
    $$\frac{27}{8} - \frac{7}{6}y > 0$$
    $$\frac{27}{8} > \frac{7}{6}y$$
    $$\frac{27}{56} > y$$
    $$y < \frac{27}{56}$$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$The equation above gives the height $h$, in feet, of a ball $t$ seconds after it is thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet. Which of the following gives $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: $v=h+k-16 t$
  B: $v=\frac{h-k+16}{t}$
  C: $v=\frac{h+k}{t}-16 t$
  D: $v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16 t$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
We are given the equation $h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$ which gives the height $h$, in feet, of a ball $t$ seconds after it is thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet.

To get $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$, we need to isolate $v$ in the given equation.

Action: 
$$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$
$$h-k=-16 t^{2}+v t$$
$$v t=h-k+16 t^{2}$$
$$v=\frac{h-k+16 t^{2}}{t}$$

Answer: Answer(B)
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The given equation is a quadratic equation in $t$.
  The coefficient of $t^2$ is negative, which means the parabola opens downwards.
  The initial velocity $v$ is the velocity at $t=0$.
  The velocity at any time $t$ is the derivative of the height function $h(t)$.
  The derivative of the given equation is $v=-32t+v_0$, where $v_0$ is the initial velocity.
  We can solve for $v_0$ by plugging in $t=0$.
Action: Answer("A")  
To find $v$, we can rearrange the derivative of the given equation to solve for $v_0$:
$$
v=-32t+v_0 \quad \Rightarrow \quad v_0=v+32t
$$
Plugging this into the original equation, we get:
$$
h=-16t^2+(v+32t)+k \quad \Rightarrow \quad h=-16t^2+v t+(32t+k)
$$
Comparing this to the given equation, we see that $k$ has been replaced by $(32t+k)$.
Therefore, we can solve for $v$ by subtracting $(32t+k)$ from both sides and dividing by $t$:
$$
h=(v-16t)+k+32t \quad \Rightarrow \quad v=h+k-16t
$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}}$.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
The given equation is a quadratic equation in $t$ with a leading coefficient of $-16$. The coefficient of $t^2$ is negative, which means the parabolic curve opens downwards. The initial velocity is $v$ and the initial height is $k$.
When the ball reaches its maximum height, its velocity is zero. 

To find the velocity $v$, we need to take the derivative of the given equation with respect to $t$. The derivative of $k$ with respect to $t$ is zero. 

$$\frac{dh}{dt}=-32t+v$$

Action: Answer("v=-32t+h+k")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  The given equation is a quadratic equation in standard form, which gives the height of a ball at any time $t$ after it is thrown straight up with an initial velocity $v$ and an initial height $k$. 
  The coefficient of $t^2$ is $-16$, which indicates that the ball is subject to a constant acceleration of $-32$ feet per second squared due to gravity.
  To find $v$, we need to isolate it on one side of the equation.

Action: 
  Rearranging the given equation, we get:
  $$h-k=-16 t^{2}+v t$$
  Adding $16t$ to both sides, we get:
  $$h-k+16t=v t$$
  Dividing both sides by $t$, we get:
  $$v=\frac{h-k+16t}{t}$$
  Therefore, the answer is (B): $v=\frac{h-k+16}{t}$.
Response 4:
Knowledge:
We are given the equation for the height of a ball thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet as: $$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$

$$h=k-16t^2+vt$$
Adding $16t^2-k$ to both sides, we get:
$$h+16t^2-k=vt$$
Dividing both sides by $t$, we get:
$$v=\frac{h+16t^2-k}{t}$$

Action: Answer("B")
Response 5:
Knowledge:
We are given the equation for the height of a ball thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet:
$$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$
We are asked to solve for $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$.

Solution:
To solve for $v$, we need to isolate $v$ on one side of the equation. We can start by subtracting $k$ from both sides of the equation:
$$h-k=-16 t^{2}+v t$$
Next, we can divide both sides by $t$:
$$\frac{h-k}{t}=-16 t+v$$
Finally, we can add $16t$ to both sides:
$$v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16t$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}\ v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16t}$.

Knowledge:
The given equation is a quadratic equation of the form $h = at^2 + bt + c$, where $a = -16$, $b = v$, and $c = k$.

To find the initial velocity $v$, we need to use the fact that the ball was thrown straight up, so its velocity at the highest point is zero. This means that the time it takes to reach the highest point is $t_{max} = \frac{v}{g}$, where $g$ is the acceleration due to gravity. At the highest point, the height of the ball is $h_{max} = h(t_{max}) = h(\frac{v}{g}) = -8 \frac{v^2}{g} + k$.

Action: 
Solve the given equation for $t_{max}$ and substitute it into the equation for $h_{max}$ to get $v$ in terms of $h$, $t$, and $k$:
$$h_{max} = -8 \frac{v^2}{g} + k$$
$$\Rightarrow v^2 = -\frac{g}{8}(h_{max} - k)$$
$$\Rightarrow v = \pm \sqrt{-\frac{g}{8}(h_{max} - k)}$$
Since the ball was thrown straight up, we take the positive square root:
$$\Rightarrow v = \sqrt{-\frac{g}{8}(h_{max} - k)}$$
Substitute $h_{max}$ and $g$ into the equation:
$$\Rightarrow v = \sqrt{32(h - k)}$$
Simplify the equation:
$$\Rightarrow v = 4\sqrt{2(h - k)}$$
$$\Rightarrow v = \frac{4\sqrt{2}}{\sqrt{t}}\sqrt{\frac{h - k}{t}}$$
$$\Rightarrow v = \frac{4\sqrt{2}}{\sqrt{t}}\sqrt{h - k}\frac{1}{\sqrt{t}}$$
$$\Rightarrow v = \frac{4\sqrt{2}}{t}\sqrt{h - k}$$

Question: $$-2 x+3 y=6$$In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is perpendicular to the graph of the equation above?

  A: $3 x+2 y=6$
  B: $3 x+4 y=6$

Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Two lines are perpendicular if and only if the product of their slopes is -1.
  The slope of a line in the form $ax+by=c$ is $-\frac{a}{b}$.
  
Action: 
  The slope of the given equation $-2x+3y=6$ is $-\frac{-2}{3}=\frac{2}{3}$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 3.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$In the system of equations above, $k$ is a constant and $x$ and $y$ are variables. For what value of $k$ will the system of equations have no solution?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{12}{5}$
  B: $\frac{16}{7}$
  C: $-\frac{16}{7}$
  D: $-\frac{12}{5}$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We can solve the system of equations by using elimination method. 
  If we multiply the first equation by $4$ and the second equation by $k$, we can eliminate $x$ by adding the two equations. 
  Then we can solve for $y$ and substitute back to find $x$.
  If the system has no solution, it means the two lines are parallel and do not intersect. This happens when the coefficients of $x$ and $y$ in the two equations are proportional to each other, but the constant terms are not proportional. 
  In other words, $\frac{4}{-5}=\frac{k}{-3}$ but $\frac{7}{-5}\neq\frac{4}{-3}$.
Action: 
  We can rewrite the equation $\frac{4}{-5}=\frac{k}{-3}$ as $k=-\frac{12}{5}$. 
  Then we can check if this value satisfies the condition $\frac{7}{-5}\neq\frac{4}{-3}$.
  We can simplify $\frac{7}{-5}$ and $\frac{4}{-3}$ as $-\frac{7}{5}$ and $-\frac{4}{3}$, respectively. 
  Since $-\frac{7}{5}\neq-\frac{4}{3}$, we have found the value of $k$ that makes the system have no solution.
  Therefore, Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We can use the determinant of the coefficient matrix to determine if the system of equations has no solution. If the determinant is 0, the system has no unique solution.
  The coefficient matrix is $\begin{pmatrix} k & -3 \\ 4 & -5 \end{pmatrix}$, and its determinant is $k(-5)-(-3)(4)=-5k+12$.
Action: 
  For the system to have no solution, the determinant must be 0. 
  So we need to solve the equation $-5k+12=0$. 
  Solving for $k$, we get $k=\frac{12}{5}$.
  Answer: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  We can solve the system of equations using elimination method. 
  Multiplying the first equation by $4$ and the second equation by $k$, we get $4kx-12y=16$ and $4kx-5ky=7k$. 
  If we subtract the second equation from the first, we get $7ky=16-7k$. 
  Therefore, $y=\frac{16-7k}{7k}$. 
  Substituting this value of $y$ in the second equation, we get $4x-5\left(\frac{16-7k}{7k}\right)=7$. 
  Simplifying this equation, we get $28kx-35(16-7k)=49k$. 
  This equation has no solution if the coefficients of $x$ are equal and the constant terms are not equal. 
  Therefore, $28k=-35$ and $49k\neq 0$. 
  Solving for $k$, we get $k=-\frac{5}{4}$.

  The slope of the line $4x-5y=7$ is $\frac{4}{5}$.

  Solving $k/3=4/5$ gives $k=12/5$.

Response 9:
Knowledge: 
  For a system of linear equations to have no solution, the lines must be parallel.
  Two lines are parallel if and only if their slopes are equal and their $y$-intercepts are different.
  The slope of a line can be found by rearranging the equation in slope-intercept form: $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the $y$-intercept.
  The slope of the line $kx-3y=4$ is $\frac{k}{3}$, and the slope of the line $4x-5y=7$ is $\frac{4}{5}$.
Action: 
  To make the system have no solution, we need the slopes to be equal and the $y$-intercepts to be different.
  The slope of the first line is $\frac{k}{3}$, and the slope of the second line is $\frac{4}{5}$. Therefore, we need $\frac{k}{3}=\frac{4}{5}$.
  Solving for $k$, we get $k=\frac{12}{5}\cdot 3 = \frac{36}{5}$.
  However, we also need the $y$-intercepts to be different. The $y$-intercept of the first line is $\frac{4}{3}$, and the $y$-intercept of the second line is $-\frac{7}{5}$. Therefore, we need $\frac{4}{3}\neq -\frac{7}{5}$.
  Since $\frac{4}{3}$ and $-\frac{7}{5}$ are different, we can conclude that the system has no solution if $k=\boxed{\textbf{(A) }\frac{12}{5}}$.
